34 
35 void CFEMStandardElementBase::IntegrationPointsLine(void) {
36 
37  /*--- Allocate the memory for the integration points
38  and weights and determine them. ---*/
39  nIntegration = orderExact/2 + 1;
40  rIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
41  wIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
42 
43  GaussLegendrePoints1D(rIntegration, wIntegration);
44 }
45 
46 void CFEMStandardElementBase::IntegrationPointsQuadrilateral(void) {
47 
48  /*--- The 2D quadrature rule is a tensor product of the 1D Gauss-Legendre
49  quadrature rule. First determine the number of integration points in 1D,
50  which is stored in M, and determine them. ---*/
51  unsigned short M = orderExact/2 + 1;
52 
53  vector<su2double> GLPoints(M), GLWeights(M);
54  GaussLegendrePoints1D(GLPoints, GLWeights);
55 
56  /*--- Allocate the memory for the integration points
57  and weights and determine them. ---*/
58  nIntegration = M*M;
59  rIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
60  sIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
61  wIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
62 
63  unsigned int ii = 0;
64  for(unsigned short j=0; j<M; ++j) {
65  for(unsigned short i=0; i<M; ++i, ++ii) {
66  rIntegration[ii] = GLPoints[i];
67  sIntegration[ii] = GLPoints[j];
68  wIntegration[ii] = GLWeights[i]*GLWeights[j];
69  }
70  }
71 }
72 
73 void CFEMStandardElementBase::IntegrationPointsPrism(void) {
74 
75  /*--- The 3D quadrature rule for a prism is a tensor product of the 1D Gauss-Legendre
76  quadrature rule with the triangle quadrature rule. Determine the number of
77  integration points in 1D, which is stored in M, and the actual integration
78  1D integration points. ---*/
79  unsigned short M = orderExact/2 + 1;
80 
81  vector<su2double> GLPoints(M), GLWeights(M);
82  GaussLegendrePoints1D(GLPoints, GLWeights);
83 
84  /*--- Also determine the integration rule for a triangle. ---*/
85  IntegrationPointsTriangle();
86 
87  unsigned short nIntTriangle = nIntegration;
88  vector<su2double> rTriangle = rIntegration;
89  vector<su2double> sTriangle = sIntegration;
90  vector<su2double> wTriangle = wIntegration;
91 
92  /*--- Allocate the memory for the integration points and weights
93  of the prism and determine them. ---*/
94  nIntegration = M*nIntTriangle;
95  rIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
96  sIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
97  tIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
98  wIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
99 
100  unsigned int ii = 0;
101  for(unsigned short k=0; k<M; ++k) {
102  for(unsigned short j=0; j<nIntTriangle; ++j, ++ii) {
103  rIntegration[ii] = rTriangle[j];
104  sIntegration[ii] = sTriangle[j];
105  tIntegration[ii] = GLPoints[k];
106  wIntegration[ii] = wTriangle[j]*GLWeights[k];
107  }
108  }
109 }
110 
111 void CFEMStandardElementBase::IntegrationPointsHexahedron(void) {
112 
113  /*--- The 3D quadrature rule is a tensor product of the 1D Gauss-Legendre
114  quadrature rule. Determine the number of integration points in 1D, which
115  is stored in M, and the actual integration 1D integration points. ---*/
116  unsigned short M = orderExact/2 + 1;
117 
118  vector<su2double> GLPoints(M), GLWeights(M);
119  GaussLegendrePoints1D(GLPoints, GLWeights);
120 
121  /*--- Allocate the memory for the integration points and weights
122  of the hexahedron and determine them. ---*/
123  nIntegration = M*M*M;
124  rIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
125  sIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
126  tIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
127  wIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
128 
129  unsigned int ii = 0;
130  for(unsigned short k=0; k<M; ++k) {
131  for(unsigned short j=0; j<M; ++j) {
132  for(unsigned short i=0; i<M; ++i, ++ii) {
133  rIntegration[ii] = GLPoints[i];
134  sIntegration[ii] = GLPoints[j];
135  tIntegration[ii] = GLPoints[k];
136  wIntegration[ii] = GLWeights[i]*GLWeights[j]*GLWeights[k];
137  }
138  }
139  }
140 }
141 
142 void CFEMStandardElementBase::IntegrationPointsTriangle(void) {
143 
144  /*--- Set the number of integration points, depending on the order of
145  polynomials that must be integrated exactly. ---*/
146  switch( orderExact ) {
147  case 0:
148  case 1: nIntegration = 1; break;
149  case 2: nIntegration = 3; break;
150  case 3:
151  case 4: nIntegration = 6; break;
152  case 5: nIntegration = 7; break;
153  case 6: nIntegration = 12; break;
154  case 7: nIntegration = 15; break;
155  case 8: nIntegration = 16; break;
156  case 9: nIntegration = 19; break;
157  case 10: nIntegration = 25; break;
158  case 11: nIntegration = 28; break;
159  case 12: nIntegration = 36; break;
160  case 13: nIntegration = 40; break;
161  case 14: nIntegration = 46; break;
162  case 15: nIntegration = 54; break;
163  case 16: nIntegration = 58; break;
164  case 17: nIntegration = 66; break;
165  case 18: nIntegration = 73; break;
166  case 19: nIntegration = 82; break;
167  case 20: nIntegration = 85; break;
168  case 21: nIntegration = 93; break;
169  case 22: nIntegration = 100; break;
170  case 23: nIntegration = 106; break;
171  case 24: nIntegration = 118; break;
172  case 25: nIntegration = 126; break;
173  case 26: nIntegration = 138; break;
174  case 27: nIntegration = 145; break;
175  case 28: nIntegration = 225; break;
176  default:
177  SU2_MPI::Error("Polynomial order not supported", CURRENT_FUNCTION);
178  }
179 
180  /*--- Allocate the memory for the integration points and their weights. ---*/
181  rIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
182  sIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
183  wIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
184 
185  /*--- Set the pointers to the data arrays of the variables just allocated, such
186  that the names are shorter. This is useful for the code below. ---*/
187  su2double *r = rIntegration.data();
188  su2double *s = sIntegration.data();
189  su2double *w = wIntegration.data();
190 
191  /*--- Set the data for the integration points, depending on the order.
192  These integration rules come from the Matlab codes corresponding to
193  the book "Nodal Discontinuous Methods: Algorithms, Analysis, and Applications"
194  by Jan S. Hesthaven and Tim Warburton. ---*/
195  switch( orderExact ) {
196  case 0:
197  case 1: {
198  r[0] = -0.333333333333333; s[0] = -0.333333333333333; w[0] = 2.000000000000000;
199 
200  break;
201  }
202  case 2: {
203  r[0] = -0.666666666666667; s[0] = -0.666666666666667; w[0] = 0.666666666666667;
204  r[1] = 0.333333333333333; s[1] = -0.666666666666667; w[1] = 0.666666666666667;
205  r[2] = -0.666666666666667; s[2] = 0.333333333333333; w[2] = 0.666666666666667;
206 
207  break;
208  }
209  case 3:
210  case 4: {

212  r[1] = 0.633695145960917; s[1] = -0.816847572980459; w[1] = 0.219903487310644;
213  r[2] = -0.816847572980459; s[2] = 0.633695145960917; w[2] = 0.219903487310644;
214  r[3] = -0.108103018168070; s[3] = -0.108103018168070; w[3] = 0.446763179356023;
215  r[4] = -0.783793963663860; s[4] = -0.108103018168070; w[4] = 0.446763179356023;
216  r[5] = -0.108103018168070; s[5] = -0.783793963663860; w[5] = 0.446763179356023;

2031 
2032 void CFEMStandardElementBase::IntegrationPointsTetrahedron(void) {
2033 
2034  /*--- Set the number of integration points, depending on the order of
2035  polynomials that must be integrated exactly. ---*/
2036  switch( orderExact ) {
2037  case 0: nIntegration = 1; break;
2038  case 1: nIntegration = 1; break;
2039  case 2: nIntegration = 4; break;
2040  case 3: nIntegration = 8; break;
2041  case 4: nIntegration = 14; break;
2042  case 5: nIntegration = 14; break;
2043  case 6: nIntegration = 24; break;
2044  case 7: nIntegration = 35; break;
2045  case 8: nIntegration = 46; break;
2046  case 9: nIntegration = 59; break;
2047  case 10: nIntegration = 81; break;
2048  case 11: nIntegration = 105; break;
2049  case 12: nIntegration = 132; break;
2050  case 13: nIntegration = 163; break;
2051  case 14: nIntegration = 214; break;
2052  case 15: nIntegration = 264; break;
2053  default:
2054  SU2_MPI::Error("Polynomial order not supported", CURRENT_FUNCTION);
2055  }
2056 
2057  /*--- Allocate the memory for the integration points and their weights. ---*/
2058  rIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
2059  sIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
2060  tIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
2061  wIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
2062 
2063  /*--- Set the pointers to the data arrays of the variables just allocated, such
2064  that the names are shorter. This is useful for the code below. ---*/
2065  su2double *r = rIntegration.data();
2066  su2double *s = sIntegration.data();
2067  su2double *t = tIntegration.data();
2068  su2double *w = wIntegration.data();
2069 
2070  /*--- Set the data for the integration points, depending on the order.
2071  These integration rules are obtained with the open source program
2072  Polyquad, developed by Freddie Witherden. ---*/
2073  switch( orderExact )
2074  {
2075  case 0:
2076  case 1: {
2077  r[0] = -0.500000000000000; s[0] = -0.500000000000000; t[0] = -0.500000000000000; w[0] = 1.333333333333333;
2078 
2079  break;
2080  }
2081  case 2: {
2082  r[0] =-0.723606797749979; s[0] = -0.723606797749979; t[0] = 0.1708203932499369; w[0] = 0.3333333333333333;
2083  r[1] =-0.723606797749979; s[1] = 0.1708203932499369; t[1] = -0.723606797749979; w[1] = 0.3333333333333333;
2084  r[2] = 0.170820393249937; s[2] = -0.723606797749979; t[2] = -0.723606797749979; w[2] = 0.3333333333333333;
2085  r[3] =-0.723606797749979; s[3] = -0.723606797749979; t[3] = -0.723606797749979; w[3] = 0.3333333333333333;
2086 
2087  break;

3285 
3286 void CFEMStandardElementBase::IntegrationPointsPyramid(void) {
3287 
3288  /*--- The 3D quadrature rule for a pyramid is obtained by transforming the
3289  standard pyramid into a standard hexahedron by means of the Duffy
3290  transformation. On the created hexahedron a tensor product rule is used,
3291  but in the t-direction a Gauss-Jacobi rule with alpha = 2, beta = 0 is
3292  used to account for the transformation from the pyramid to the
3293  hexahedron. The determinant of the Jacobian of this transformation
3294  is 0.25*(1-t)^2, which explains the alpha = 2 in the Gauss-Jacobi.
3295  Determine the number of integration points in 1D, which is stored in M,
3296  and the actual integration 1D integration points. ---*/
3297  unsigned short M = orderExact/2 + 1;
3298 
3299  vector<su2double> GLPoints(M), GLWeights(M);
3300  GaussLegendrePoints1D(GLPoints, GLWeights);
3301 
3302  vector<passivedouble> GJPoints(M), GJWeights(M);
3303  CGaussJacobiQuadrature GaussJacobi;
3304  GaussJacobi.GetQuadraturePoints(2.0, 0.0, -1.0, 1.0, GJPoints, GJWeights);
3305 
3306  /*--- Allocate the memory for the integration points and weights
3307  of the pyramid and determine them. ---*/
3308  nIntegration = M*M*M;
3309  rIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
3310  sIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
3311  tIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
3312  wIntegration.resize(nIntegration);
3313 
3314  unsigned int ii = 0;
3315  for(unsigned short k=0; k<M; ++k) {
3316  for(unsigned short j=0; j<M; ++j) {
3317  for(unsigned short i=0; i<M; ++i, ++ii) {
3318  const su2double xi = GLPoints[i];
3319  const su2double eta = GLPoints[j];
3320  const su2double zeta = GJPoints[k];
3321  rIntegration[ii] = 0.5*(1.0-zeta)*xi;
3322  sIntegration[ii] = 0.5*(1.0-zeta)*eta;
3323  tIntegration[ii] = zeta;
3324  wIntegration[ii] = 0.25*GLWeights[i]*GLWeights[j]*GJWeights[k];
3325  }
3326  }
3327  }
3328 }
